Below is a **GitHub-ready RFC + patent-style specification** focused specifically on **AppCraft.scan()**, anchored within the broader **Corpdesk automation mechanism** and explicitly tying to your `app-craft.model.ts` interfaces and `ICdRequest/ICdResponse` via **CdWire**.

---

# 📄 RFC-00XX: AppCraft Scan — Directory Signature Extraction & Conformity Analysis

## Status

Draft

## Author

Corpdesk Architecture

## Date

2026-03-28

---

# 1. Abstract

This document defines the **AppCraft Scan Mechanism**, a core capability within the Corpdesk automation framework responsible for:

* **Analyzing an existing application directory**
* **Transforming it into a structured, machine-readable descriptor (`CdAppDescriptor`)**
* **Generating a formal directory signature (`DirectorySignatureDescriptor`)**
* **Evaluating conformity against Corpdesk architectural conventions**
* **Returning results via `ICdResponse` under the CdWire protocol**

The scan operation establishes the **foundation for automated development**, enabling:

* Structural validation
* Automated refactoring
* Reverse engineering into Corpdesk-compliant systems
* AI-assisted development workflows

---

# 2. Motivation

Modern software systems lack a **formalized structural DNA representation**.

The AppCraft Scan introduces:

* A **canonical tree representation** of applications
* A **mathematical mapping of structure → meaning**
* A **bidirectional transformation model**:

  * Scan (Physical → Descriptor)
  * Create (Descriptor → Physical)

This enables Corpdesk to operate as a:

> **Self-aware software automation system**

---

# 3. Scope

This RFC defines:

* The **AppCraft.scan() operation**
* The **data structures used to represent scanned systems**
* The **evaluation model (Conformity + Infection)**
* The **integration with CdWire (`ICdRequest/ICdResponse`)**
* The role of **SeedConfig and expression metadata**

---

# 4. Definitions

| Term                | Description                                                              |
| ------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------ |
| Scan                | Process of analyzing a filesystem and generating a structured descriptor |
| Descriptor          | A structured representation of an application (`CdAppDescriptor`)        |
| Directory Signature | A recursive tree representation (`DirectorySignatureDescriptor`)         |
| Node                | A file or directory (`DirectoryNode`)                                    |
| Conformity (CR)     | Measure of alignment with Corpdesk conventions                           |
| Infection (I)       | Measure of structural deviation                                          |
| Genome (Γ)          | `.cd/cd-app.descriptor.json`                                             |
| Dimensionality (Σ)  | Expected structural expansion (e.g., Controller/Service/Model)           |

---

# 5. Architectural Position

The scan operation exists within:

```
cd-cli → DevMode → AppCraft → CdAppController.scan()
```

And communicates via:

* `ICdRequest`
* `ICdResponse`
* under the **CdWire protocol**

---

# 6. Request Model (CdWire)

## 6.1 ICdRequest

```ts
{
  ctx: "app",
  m: "app-craft",
  c: "CdApp",
  a: "scan",
  dat: {
    f_vals: [...],
    token: string | null
  },
  args: {
    actionTargetName: "cd-app",
    name: string,
    oEnv: string,
    repo: string
  }
}
```

---

# 7. Response Model (CdWire)

## 7.1 ICdResponse

```ts
{
  app_state: IAppState,
  data: {
    descriptor: CdAppDescriptor,
    audit?: ScanAuditResult
  }
}
```

---

## 7.2 ScanAuditResult (Derived)

```ts
interface ScanAuditResult {
  conformityScore: number;   // CR
  infectionScore: number;    // I
  totalNodes: number;
  matchedNodes: number;
  anomalies?: string[];
}
```

---

# 8. Core Descriptor Model

## 8.1 CdAppDescriptor

```ts
export interface CdAppDescriptor {
  name: string;
  modules: CdModuleDescriptor[];
  directorySignature?: DirectorySignatureDescriptor;
  environments?: EnvironmentDescriptor[];
  versionControl?: VersionControlDescriptor;
}
```

### Role

Represents the **complete structural and semantic identity** of an application.

---

## 8.2 DirectorySignatureDescriptor

```ts
export interface DirectorySignatureDescriptor {
  signatureName: string;
  root: DirectoryNode;
  variables?: Record<string, string>;
}
```

### Role

Represents the **formal tree structure** of the application.

---

## 8.3 DirectoryNode

```ts
export interface DirectoryNode {
  name: string;
  cdObjGuid: string;
  cdObjRoleName?: string;
  weight?: number;
  isFile?: boolean;
  templateRef?: string;
  children?: DirectoryNode[];
}
```

### Role

Represents a **single structural unit** (file or directory).

---

# 9. Scan Processing Pipeline

## 9.1 Stage 1 — Initialization

* Resolve project (`name`, `repo`)
* Validate environment (`oEnv`)
* Load `SeedConfig`

---

## 9.2 Stage 2 — Directory Traversal

Recursive scan:

* Include: source files
* Ignore:

  * `node_modules`
  * `.git`
  * build directories

Output:

```
Flat list of filesystem entries
```

---

## 9.3 Stage 3 — Node Construction

Transform filesystem → `DirectoryNode` tree

```ts
DirectoryNode {
  name,
  isFile,
  children[]
}
```

---

## 9.4 Stage 4 — Role Attribution

Using `SeedConfig.roles` and expressions:

Example:

```ts
if (fileName === "main.ts") → role = "Origin"
if (path.includes("/controllers/")) → role = "Controller"
```


---

# 🔹 9.5 Stage 5 — Weight Assignment (Expanded)

## 9.5.1 Overview

Weight Assignment is the process of attributing **quantitative significance** to each `DirectoryNode` based on its **architectural role**, **structural importance**, and **compliance relevance**.

Unlike conventional scanners that perform **binary validation (pass/fail)**, the AppCraft Scan introduces a **continuous scoring model**, enabling nuanced evaluation of application structures.

---

## 9.5.2 Rationale

### 1. Limitations of Conventional Scanners

Traditional directory analyzers and linters typically:

* Validate **presence/absence** of files
* Enforce **static rules**
* Produce **boolean outputs**:

  * ✅ Valid
  * ❌ Invalid

This approach has inherent limitations:

| Limitation        | Impact                                                  |
| ----------------- | ------------------------------------------------------- |
| Binary evaluation | Cannot express partial correctness                      |
| No prioritization | All violations treated equally                          |
| Low adaptability  | Difficult to apply across diverse codebases             |
| Poor guidance     | Does not indicate *how close* a system is to compliance |

---

### 2. Need for Gradual Compliance Measurement

Real-world systems:

* Are often **partially compliant**
* Evolve incrementally
* Require **progressive alignment**, not abrupt rejection

Therefore, a **graded evaluation system** is required.

---

## 9.5.3 Core Concept

Each node is assigned a **weight (W)**:

```id="4m8ybt"
DirectoryNode.weight ∈ ℝ⁺
```

Weights represent:

* Structural importance
* Architectural criticality
* Contribution to overall compliance

---

## 9.5.4 Weight Categories

| Category         | Example                              | Weight Range | Significance           |
| ---------------- | ------------------------------------ | ------------ | ---------------------- |
| Critical Nodes   | `main.ts`, `.cd/app-descriptor.json` | 9–10         | Define system identity |
| Structural Nodes | `sys/`, `app/`, `utils/`             | 6–9          | Define architecture    |
| Functional Nodes | controllers, services, models        | 7–8          | Define behavior        |
| Auxiliary Nodes  | scripts, configs                     | 3–6          | Support system         |
| Unknown Nodes    | unrecognized files                   | 0–2          | Potential deviation    |

---

## 9.5.5 Conformity as a Continuous Function

Instead of:

```id="skj5z5"
isValid = true | false
```

AppCraft defines:

```id="v0n9ql"
CR = Σ(W_matched) / Σ(W_expected)
```

Where:

* `CR ∈ [0,1]`
* Represents **degree of compliance**

---

## 9.5.6 Threshold-Based Compliance

This enables **practical decision-making**:

| CR Range    | Interpretation                |
| ----------- | ----------------------------- |
| ≥ 0.90      | Fully compliant               |
| 0.75 – 0.89 | Acceptable (minor deviations) |
| 0.50 – 0.74 | Needs alignment               |
| < 0.50      | Non-compliant                 |

### Key Advantage

> Compliance is **not binary**, but **threshold-driven**

This allows:

* Gradual adoption of Corpdesk
* Realistic evaluation of legacy systems
* Controlled enforcement policies

---

## 9.5.7 Infection Metric (Complementary)

Weighting also enables **negative signal detection**:

```id="7r3p7f"
I = V(χ) / V(total)
```

Where:

* `χ` = set of anomalous nodes

This captures:

* Structural pollution
* Non-standard patterns
* Unregistered modules

---

## 9.5.8 Significance in Corpdesk Architecture

Weight Assignment transforms the scan into:

### 1. A Measurable System

* Every structure becomes **quantifiable**
* Enables analytics and benchmarking

---

### 2. A Guidance System

Instead of:

> “Invalid structure”

AppCraft provides:

> “You are 82% compliant — missing high-weight nodes: base.service.ts, descriptor file”

---

### 3. A Feedback Loop

Supports:

* Continuous improvement
* CI/CD integration
* Automated refactoring triggers

---

## 9.5.9 Uniqueness and Novelty

The AppCraft weighting model introduces several novel aspects:

---

### (a) Structural Semantics Encoding

Weights are not arbitrary:

* They encode **architectural meaning**
* Derived from Corpdesk roles:

  * Origin (O)
  * Genome (Γ)
  * Substrate (S)
  * Agency (A)
  * Utility (U)

---

### (b) Mathematical Representation of Software Structure

The system models applications as:

```id="pd9b03"
Application Score = f(Σ, Γ, Roles, Weights)
```

This bridges:

* Filesystem structure
* Mathematical formalism

---

### (c) Continuous Compliance Spectrum

Unlike conventional tools:

* No rigid pass/fail boundary
* Supports **adaptive thresholds**

---

### (d) AI-Ready Scoring System

Weights act as:

* **Feature signals** for AI models
* Inputs for:

  * Prompt generation
  * Code synthesis decisions
  * Refactoring prioritization

---

### (e) Bidirectional Utility

Weights are used in:

| Direction | Role                  |
| --------- | --------------------- |
| Scan      | Evaluate structure    |
| Create    | Prioritize generation |
| AI        | Guide reasoning       |

---

## 9.5.10 Extended Interpretations

Beyond compliance, weights enable:

---

### 1. Structural Density

```id="6f0jso"
Density = Σ(W_nodes) / totalNodes
```

Measures:

* Architectural richness
* Design maturity

---

### 2. Critical Path Identification

Identify:

* High-weight nodes missing or incorrect

---

### 3. Evolution Tracking

Compare scans over time:

```id="mw9x8q"
ΔCR = CR_t2 - CR_t1
```

Used for:

* Progress measurement
* CI/CD gating

---

### 4. Module-Level Scoring

Apply CR per module:

```id="xf2r0h"
CR_module = Σ(W_module_matched) / Σ(W_module_expected)
```

Enables:

* Targeted improvements
* Selective refactoring

---

## 9.5.11 Patent Considerations (Weighting Model)

### Claim Extension

The system introduces:

> A method of assigning weighted architectural significance to filesystem elements, enabling continuous compliance scoring and adaptive threshold-based validation.

Key differentiators:

* Use of **role-based weights**
* Integration with **recursive directory signatures**
* Application of **continuous scoring instead of discrete validation**

---

## 9.5.12 Summary

Weight Assignment is the **core differentiator** of AppCraft Scan:

| Traditional Scanner | AppCraft Scan              |
| ------------------- | -------------------------- |
| Boolean validation  | Continuous scoring         |
| Static rules        | Weighted semantics         |
| Pass/Fail           | Threshold-based compliance |
| No prioritization   | Importance-driven analysis |
| Limited AI use      | AI-native scoring          |

---

## 🔥 Strategic Insight

This section is what makes Corpdesk:

> Not just a framework
> but a **computable model of software architecture**

---

If you want next, we can:

* Formalize the **weight system as equations (for your mathematical layer)**
* Or map weights directly into your **ExpressionMetadata → scoringWeights**
* Or plug this into actual code inside `scan()` step-by-step

This is now the **intelligence core** of the entire system.


---

## 9.6 Stage 6 — Signature Construction

```ts
DirectorySignatureDescriptor {
  signatureName: "<app>-scan",
  root: DirectoryNode
}
```

---

## 9.7 Stage 7 — Descriptor Assembly

```ts
CdAppDescriptor {
  name,
  modules,
  directorySignature
}
```

---

## 9.8 Stage 8 — Audit Computation

### Conformity (CR)

```
CR = Σ(weight of valid nodes) / Σ(total possible weight)
```

### Infection (I)

```
I = invalidNodes / totalNodes
```

---

## 9.9 Stage 9 — Persistence

Write to:

```
<root>/.cd/cd-app.descriptor.json
```

---

## 9.10 Stage 10 — Response Return

Return via `ICdResponse`

---

# 10. SeedConfig Integration

## 10.1 Purpose

Defines **expected structure and rules**

```ts
export interface SeedConfig {
  subsystemName: string;
  roles: SeedRoleConfig[];
  ignorePatterns?: string[];
  expressionMetadata?: ExpressionMetadata;
}
```

---

## 10.2 Role Mapping

```ts
export interface SeedRoleConfig {
  roleName: string;
  namingPattern?: string;
  expression?: string;
  weight?: number;
}
```

---

## 10.3 Expression Engine

Supports:

```
file.name CONTAINS '.controller.'
path INCLUDES '/services/'
```

---

# 11. Mathematical Foundation

The scan aligns with Corpdesk formalism:

```
Application = f(O, S ∪ A ∪ U, Σ, Γ)
```

Where:

* **O** = Origin (`main.ts`)
* **S** = Substrate (`sys/`)
* **A** = Agency (`app/`)
* **U** = Utility (`utils/`)
* **Σ** = Dimensionality (Controller/Service/Model)
* **Γ** = Genome (`.cd/app-descriptor.json`)

---

# 12. Output Example

```json
{
  "name": "cd-cli",
  "directorySignature": {
    "signatureName": "cd-cli-scan",
    "root": {
      "name": "cd-cli",
      "children": [
        {
          "name": "src",
          "children": [
            {
              "name": "main.ts",
              "isFile": true,
              "cdObjRoleName": "Origin",
              "weight": 10
            }
          ]
        }
      ]
    }
  }
}
```

---

# 13. Patent Claims (Draft)

## Claim 1

A method for transforming a filesystem into a structured descriptor using weighted role attribution.

## Claim 2

A system for evaluating software conformity using mathematical scoring derived from structural roles.

## Claim 3

A bidirectional transformation system enabling:

* Directory → Descriptor (Scan)
* Descriptor → Directory (Create)

## Claim 4

An AI-integrated architecture where descriptors serve as prompt seeds for automated code generation.

---

# 14. Future Extensions

* Reverse generation (`create`)
* AI agent integration
* Multi-language support
* Dynamic rule learning

---

# 15. Conclusion

The AppCraft Scan mechanism establishes:

* A **formal representation of software structure**
* A **measurable compliance system**
* A **foundation for AI-driven development**

It is the **entry point into Corpdesk’s automated software lifecycle**.
